Output only the translation. <NL> English: which was a problem, given that the Fiat board had just decreed that all future Alfa's <NL> Spanish:	 ¿cuál era un problema, dado que el Consejo de Fiat había acabado de decretar que todos los futuros Alfas <NL> In this case, the sentence has a subject ("which"), an auxiliary verb ("was"), and a verb ("a problem"). The noun phrase "a problem" is a nominalization of the verb "to be a problem". In Spanish, nominalizations usually end in -o (for masculine subjects) or -a (for feminine or neutral subjects), and are followed by an article if necessary. Here, since "which" (uno/una in Spanish) is masculine, we use the masculine form "-o", and since it's a noun, we add an article ("el"): "el problema". In this case, because the sentence has already been nominalized, we don't need to repeat the auxiliary verb when translating. So the translation is: "el problema, dado que el Consejo de Fiat había acabado de decretar que todos los futuros Alfas" (which was a problem, given that the Fiat board had just decreed that all future Alfa's).
